<div id="review_231950953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231950953" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523632271p2/5004971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231950953?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231950953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11028049797069104944">Big and dense and complicated and really, really, really good.<br/><br/>This is our first <i>real</i> visit to Union; specifically, the capital planet Cyteen (less habitable for humans than either Pell or Earth, but, unlike Pell, unencumbered by intelligent natives so they can start seriously terraforming; but that's really almost entirely secondary to the story), even more specifically, the administrative offices and laboratories of Reseune, the corporation (which, in this context, means quasi-independent, a se</span>
  <span id="freeText11028049797069104944" style="display:none">Big and dense and complicated and really, really, really good.<br /><br />This is our first <i>real</i> visit to Union; specifically, the capital planet Cyteen (less habitable for humans than either Pell or Earth, but, unlike Pell, unencumbered by intelligent natives so they can start seriously terraforming; but that's really almost entirely secondary to the story), even more specifically, the administrative offices and laboratories of Reseune, the corporation (which, in this context, means quasi-independent, a self-governing entity within Union) that manufactures the azi, the cloned and tape-trained servant class upon which Union's expansion has been built, plus various other projects having to do with psychset manipulation and with cloning and genetic modification, and most specifically, to Arianne Emory, head of Reseune, brilliant, single-minded, and (not to put too fine a point on it) something of a monster, caught up in political infighting in the Union council and bureaucratic infighting within Reseune itself.<br /><br />Until she's murdered about 100 pages into this 680 page novel.<br /><br />At which point the focus shifts to the two characters who will be the poles of the book -- Ari 2 (a Personal Replicate (PR), an exact genetic clone of the original Ariane Emory, whose gestation was set in motion at the original's death, and Justin Warrick, himself a PR of one of Ariane's fellow researchers, and whom Ariane, when he was young and vulnerable, took unconscionable liberties with (which action may or may not have precipitated Ariane's murder?).<br /><br />As Ari 2 grows up (a frighteningly bright and not altogether nice child) she becomes aware that she is <i>not like</i> the other children in her orbit; and she and Justin find themselves caught between Ari 1's design and the machinations of those (internal and external) who did <i>not</i> approve of Ari 1's work and/or who just want to secure power for themselves.<br /><br />This certainly works well as a standalone, but I'd recommend reading at least <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/57045.Downbelow_Station__The_Company_Wars___1_" title="Downbelow Station (The Company Wars, #1) by C.J. Cherryh" rel="nofollow noopener">Downbelow Station</a> (which provides broad context for the setting) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/57148.Forty_Thousand_in_Gehenna__Unionside___1_" title="Forty Thousand in Gehenna (Unionside, #1) by C.J. Cherryh" rel="nofollow noopener">Forty Thousand in Gehenna</a> (because the Gehenna project features prominently in Cyteen; and it's fascinating to reconsider 40,000 in Gehenna based on the new information found in Cyteen) beforehand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11028049797069104944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1450701934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1450701934" />
    <a title="Edwin Priest" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15654942-edwin-priest"><img alt="Edwin Priest" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447291259p2/15654942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1450701934?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edwin Priest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edwin Priest" href="/user/show/15654942-edwin-priest">Edwin Priest</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1450701934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4801549796375732993"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/834518.Cyteen__Cyteen___1_3_' title='Cyteen (Cyteen, #1-3) by C.J. Cherryh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cyteen</a> is one of the more frustrating books I have read recently. It is on the one hand brilliant and packed with thought provoking intellection, and on the other hand, a plodding and ponderous book in which very little happens and which I found a chore to read.<br/><br/>This book is deep and sweeping, and the points for discussion are innumerable. Clearly at the center are the concepts of how we come to be who we are, the whole nature versus nurture concept, the essence of how we are shaped and learn. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/989968.C_J__Cherryh' title='C.J. Cherryh' rel='nofollow noopener'>C.</a></span>
  <span id="freeText4801549796375732993" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/834518.Cyteen__Cyteen___1_3_" title="Cyteen (Cyteen, #1-3) by C.J. Cherryh" rel="nofollow noopener">Cyteen</a> is one of the more frustrating books I have read recently. It is on the one hand brilliant and packed with thought provoking intellection, and on the other hand, a plodding and ponderous book in which very little happens and which I found a chore to read.<br /><br />This book is deep and sweeping, and the points for discussion are innumerable. Clearly at the center are the concepts of how we come to be who we are, the whole nature versus nurture concept, the essence of how we are shaped and learn. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/989968.C_J__Cherryh" title="C.J. Cherryh" rel="nofollow noopener">C.J. Cherryh</a> delves deeply into how the manipulation of our environment and psyche can influence us. She seems to have been heavily influenced in this by the psychiatric psychotherapy concepts of Cognitive-behavioral therapy and hypnotherapy. She talks of “endocrine learning” clearly drawing on Pavlovian influences. She does this fairly brilliantly, centering around the concepts of cloning. Can a clone, even when the genetic and environmental upbringing are identically recreated, ever be a true duplicate of the original?<br /><br />Cyteen is also a complex commentary about the psychological effects and use of power and manipulation. Ari, the central character in this book, is in particular a master of this. She is able to read, control and exploit those around her, and she often takes this beyond the limits of what is right.<br /><br />Cherryh is much like Margaret Atwood in that the science in this book, although certainly often a springboard for her ideas, serves mostly as a backdrop to the more import human messages she is conveying. This is not hard science fiction, and in many ways it feels as though she has simply moved our current world and social structures, with all of their warts and problems, into a different, but mostly the same, other place. It just doesn't feel like the 25th century.<br /><br />Where this book fell down for me is the pacing and length. It is long and feels long. There are plodding sections of political machinations and long stretches of self-analysis and introspection on the part of the main characters Ari and Justin. And generally, there is just no movement in this book. I frequently found myself counting the number of pages that I had left, never a good sign.<br /><br />So I rate this book three very conflicted stars. It is a difficult and slow read, long and boring, yet chocked full of brilliance and insight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4801549796375732993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer719580648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8367426786344129189">This is only my second C.J. Cherryh novel, and I liked it very much. I found it to be a more intimate, character-driven story than <i>Downbelow Station</i>.<br/><br/>This takes place almost entirely at a research institute called Reseune which specializes in human cloning. They also produce special clones known as “Azi” who are subjected to intense conditioning from birth which gives them a different psychological makeup from regular humans. The Azi exist largely as an enslaved workforce. <br/><br/>I suppose enslaved is t</span>
  <span id="freeText8367426786344129189" style="display:none">This is only my second C.J. Cherryh novel, and I liked it very much. I found it to be a more intimate, character-driven story than <i>Downbelow Station</i>.<br /><br />This takes place almost entirely at a research institute called Reseune which specializes in human cloning. They also produce special clones known as “Azi” who are subjected to intense conditioning from birth which gives them a different psychological makeup from regular humans. The Azi exist largely as an enslaved workforce. <br /><br />I suppose enslaved is the correct word, because while they aren’t physically forced or confined, they are psychologically unable to displease their supervisors. It’s a weird and fascinating setup, because the Azi are intelligent and not discontented, and none of the characters seem to be bothered by what feels to the reader like horrifying mind control.<br /><br />The novel is about Reseune’s attempt to recreate genius: simply cloning a genius hasn't produced satisfactory results, so now they're trying to raise such a clone in a duplicate of the social and educational environment of the original.<br /><br />We follow the clone of Ariane Emory, a scary, brilliant scientist and powerful political leader, from birth through her adolescence. Since the human lifespan has been extended to around 140 years, most of the people who knew the first version of the woman are still around to be made nervous by the prospect of a second one.<br /><br />In particular the story focuses on Justin, a cloned “parental replicate” of his scientist father, and Grant, an Azi created to be Justin’s companion. Justin was psychologically damaged by the first Ariane Emory, and he and Grant spend anguished decades as victims of a tense political environment, waiting for the new one to grow up and make things worse.<br /><br />I have already ordered several more books set in this universe, including the immediate sequel to this one, which was published several years later.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8367426786344129189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7151234234886951232">A truly extraordinary book. Cherryh's insights into "tape" and "deep tape" (much like hypnosis) for training and learning are amazing. Her presentation of politics, psychology and human emotion and failings are wonderful, and her prose is some of the finest around.<br/><br/>I loved the "Boys from Brazil" theme in the book; the re-creation of a person without "magical knowledge transfer" but through re-creation of childhood environments and deep hypnotic training of a life recorded closely.<br/><br/>The social issue</span>
  <span id="freeText7151234234886951232" style="display:none">A truly extraordinary book. Cherryh's insights into "tape" and "deep tape" (much like hypnosis) for training and learning are amazing. Her presentation of politics, psychology and human emotion and failings are wonderful, and her prose is some of the finest around.<br /><br />I loved the "Boys from Brazil" theme in the book; the re-creation of a person without "magical knowledge transfer" but through re-creation of childhood environments and deep hypnotic training of a life recorded closely.<br /><br />The social issues of creating test-tube humans ("Azis") for use to populate worlds quickly (for political ends) and as servants are presented very skilfully, and with great compassion.<br /><br />The brutal manipulation of those surrounding the central character are so well-presented that you agonise with them. Plot twists are fully believable, and move the story along, especially in the last 1/4 of the book.<br /><br />Characters presented here are complex, with strengths and flaws, redemption and failure, love and broken egos. Superb.<br /><br />This is a brilliant mind writing at it's peak powers. I can't wait to continue with Regenesis.<br /><br />Definitely read Forty Thousand in Gehenna first. Reading the other Union-Alliance stories prior to this one will improve your appreciation here.<br /><br /><br />Winner: Hugo Award for Best Novel<br /><br />Winner: Locus Award Best Novel<br /><br />Nominee: British Science Ficion Award<br /><br />Number 30 on Locus list of All Time Best SF Novels.<br /><br />For Cherryh, the Alliance-Union universe books are (mostly) fantastic -<br />* In order to read:<br /><br />Downbelow Station (1981) - Superb!!<br />Merchanter's Luck (1982) - Perhaps her best ever!<br />Rimrunners (1989) – Very good!<br />Heavy Time (1991) - good, but long winded<br />Hellburner (1992) - good, but long winded<br />Tripoint (1994) - very good<br />Finity's End (1997) – Superb<br />Forty Thousand in Gehenna (1983) - good but uneven, important for Cyteen and Regenesis<br />Cyteen (1988) – Superb<br />Regenesis (2009) - Superb</span>

<div id="review_2485964387" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VexenReplica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VexenReplica" href="/user/show/85096106-vexenreplica">VexenReplica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2485964387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6836911191573975517">Thanks to Strix to reccing this to me, as it fits my /r/fantasy bingo square for user rec. 4.25/5 stars, rounded down.<br/><br/>CW for rape. (one scene with long-lasting implications)<br/><br/>Deep, dense, and thick as a brick, Cyteen is like Huxley's <i>Brave New World</i> on steroids mixed with a dash of Asimov's <i>Foundation</i>. It follows the lives of three PRs (basically clones) of very intelligent and powerful humans. It is a story about their growth and development, but it is most certainly not centered on that. There's</span>
  <span id="freeText6836911191573975517" style="display:none">Thanks to Strix to reccing this to me, as it fits my /r/fantasy bingo square for user rec. 4.25/5 stars, rounded down.<br /><br />CW for rape. (one scene with long-lasting implications)<br /><br />Deep, dense, and thick as a brick, Cyteen is like Huxley's <i>Brave New World</i> on steroids mixed with a dash of Asimov's <i>Foundation</i>. It follows the lives of three PRs (basically clones) of very intelligent and powerful humans. It is a story about their growth and development, but it is most certainly not centered on that. There's political scheming, manuvering, and all sorts of interesting commentary about AI-esque clones versus their "human" counterparts. <br /><br />The book is long and dense. This is not a book that I stretched out because I wanted it to last but rather due to its content and how it is presented. Imo, it is very difficult, at least in the first 60-ish percent, to read more than a section at a time due to the density and complicated story Cherryh is telling. (I am certainly sure this book has a delightful amount of content that pops out on a reread) The last thirty-ish percent definitely ramps up in pace, and Cherryh turns up the speed (and stakes) of the narrative. It's like all of the bits and pieces you've been learning about come together in a wonderful mixture. However, this creates an oddly tonally different story than the first bit, which personally I didn't mind but may cause issues for those who thrive on worldbuilding and character/idea exploration.<br /><br />Characters were fully fleshed out. Idea generation (for the cloning and 'tapes,' the equivalent of machine learning) was top-notch, although the technology is certainly of its era (lol faxing). Pacing was slow up until the aforementioned thirtyish percent left, where the pace really started to pick up, and then it was FULL STEAM AHEAD. There is a complexity to this book that I don't think I fully grasped, but I am not mentally ready for a reread anytime in the near future. This is not a popcorn read. Yes, the book is dense, but there is so much good in the book.<br /><br />For those playing bingo, this fits for AI, maybe cyberpunk, local for those in St. Louis, Missouri (USA) area, according to isfdb, and Strix will shill it to you nonstop, so it covers your rec square. There is a fourth book, <i>Regenesis</i>, not part of this collection, which qualifies you for final book (afaik).<br /><br />It's a tough book, but it may be well worth your time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6836911191573975517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5594518541519225568" style="display:none">I liked this book. I even think it's four stars because I was so interested in the character of Ari2. Great worldbuilding. But pacing was poor. <br /><br />I think that the amount of lip biting that went on was ridiculous. There are other reactions to stress and emotion. All the characters' lips should have been scarred for life. <br /><br />And after I read ALL THAT, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the end was kind of a letdown. <span id="freeTextContainer16905004503019831328">It feels pretty late to be reviewing this novel close to thirty years after its publication, so review it I won't. I'll just jot down a few notes. <br/><br/>This is my first novel by Cherryh and I had very little idea what to expect other than knowing it would have a raped male charater.   <span id="freeText16905004503019831328" style="display:none">It feels pretty late to be reviewing this novel close to thirty years after its publication, so review it I won't. I'll just jot down a few notes. <br /><br />This is my first novel by Cherryh and I had very little idea what to expect other than knowing it would have a raped male charater. I do want to say that it's dense and hugely satisfying, that it takes on terribly difficult subjects and (mostly) does them justice, and that I loved how it was sprawling and strangely paced (the events <i>from the blurb</i> take place 100+ pages in!), while at the same time commanding my complete attention. It seemed to me to be very different from how novels are written these days, but instead of feeling old-fashioned it felt original and powerful.<br /><br />And now, the jotted notes:<br /><br />It is a novel about consent, taking place in a society built in large part by means of slavery and rape and I don't think this should be downplayed. <br /><br />I have my own theory re: the murder mystery <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and I don't know if the sequel bears me out, but to me Ari senior seems to be the most likely suspect in her own murder, one way or another. Faced with certainty of impending death and risk that Jordan will continue to influence Justin, she chose to speed up the development of her clone while in one fell swoop removing Jordan from power. This was my first guess and I'm not sure there's any definitive proof to the contrary in Cyteen. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I found the manner in which Nyes raised and abused Ari to be utterly terrifying. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean, the endocrine element seemed a little exaggerated/dubious, a product of its time, perhaps, but the idea that they basically collaborate in making her into a sexual predator (because Ariane Senior was one, and <i>what if that was part of what made her a genius</i> and also maybe that'll be helpful in handling her) was horrifying. Plus the manner in which elites worked to cover up abuse because it was treated as the price of brilliance (neither Ari understands easily being said "no" to; of course they like best those who don't have the ability to object). And the fact that so many characters have azi "companions" (which, of course they would, that's part of the sociogeny/psychogeny/Ariane's design for the future of humankind). There are so many scenes where Cherryh has CIT characters tell AZIs to perform emotional, sexual and physical labour for them and I have little doubt every time Ari tells Florian to "do something" for her, we are reading about rape, and the way Cherryh writes it doesn't hide it. I found Florian and Catlin's storyline heartbreaking, but Grant's too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Halfway through the book, I ordered some more Cherryh novels online and now look forward to receiving them. Who knew reading old school sff could be so amazing! (I knew, I totally knew.)</span>

<div id="review_140665618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140665618" />
    <a title="Lis Carey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3726509-lis-carey"><img alt="Lis Carey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295004130p2/3726509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140665618?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lis Carey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lis Carey" href="/user/show/3726509-lis-carey">Lis Carey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/16143377-cyteen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3726509-lis-carey?shelf=f-sf">f-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3726509-lis-carey?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3726509-lis-carey?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140665618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17253170814755072316">I will confess it up front. I love this book.<br/><br/>Yes, it's long. It was originally published in three volumes in paperback, in the late 1980s. That made sense from a physical size point of view; it doesn't make sense in terms of the story. This is, like The Lord of the Rings, a long, single novel.<br/><br/>It is, as another review commented, a murder mystery in which the mystery is never solved, and features a conspiracy which is partially but never completely explained. We don't get all the answers.<br/><br/>That's pa</span>
  <span id="freeText17253170814755072316" style="display:none">I will confess it up front. I love this book.<br /><br />Yes, it's long. It was originally published in three volumes in paperback, in the late 1980s. That made sense from a physical size point of view; it doesn't make sense in terms of the story. This is, like The Lord of the Rings, a long, single novel.<br /><br />It is, as another review commented, a murder mystery in which the mystery is never solved, and features a conspiracy which is partially but never completely explained. We don't get all the answers.<br /><br />That's part of what makes it the fascinating, complex book that it is.<br /><br />Ariane Emory is over a century old, a scientist, head of Reseune, the primary cloning facility on Cyteen, the primary planet of the political entity Union, in Cherryh's Union-Alliance universe. Union and Alliance have a lot of reasons for their conflict, but one of them is the azi, Reseune's clones. Along with being genetically designed to have certain aptitudes and traits, they are also tape-trained from birth to both educate and condition them to their intended roles. They don't have a normal range of free will, though neither are they anything close to automata. There's also internal conflict, both inside Union, and inside Reseune. We see Ariane Emory, or Ari, as very intelligent, very capable, with what may be good goals, but very, very Machiavellian. She's involved in a contest of will that in part involves another clone designer, Jordan Warrick, his cloned son Justin (a clone, but not an azi; Justin is a citizen), and Justin's azi companion, Grant.<br /><br />And then, quite suddenly, Ari is dead, and it appears to be murder, and of all the people who might have wanted her dead, Jordan Warrick is the one who was there.<br /><br />The bulk of this novel is about Ari II, a clone of Ariane Emory, initially a deep, deep secret. She's not just a clone, like Justin. She's intended to be a true recreation of Ariane Emory, with all her abilities and ruthlessness.<br /><br />It's not the plotters we identify with. It is, on the one hand, Justin and Grant, living under constant suspicion and surveillance, and on the other hand, Ari II, struggling to understand how she's being manipulated and why. As a young child, friends she has too much conflict with disappear, they and their families being transferred to distant locations like Fargone Station. Her Maman, Jane Stassen, gets transferred to Fargone without Ari, when she's barely preteen, for reasons that never make sense to her. Her uncles, Denis and Geraud Nye, major powers in Reseune, are her guardians--and Denis at least seems loving and kind, but even at this young age she knows there's more going on than she's being told.<br /><br />It's not clear how much the Nyes and their allies understood how determined and devious young Ari would be in looking for the answers.<br /><br />And along the way, Ari is introduced to the resources Ari I left behind for her, because Ari did plan this even if her death didn't happen as she anticipated, and we start to learn a great deal more about the original Ari, about Reseune, about Union, and about the Nyes.<br /><br />Ari II also starts to acquire friends and allies of her own.<br /><br />Everyone here is more complicated, layered, and conflicted than they appear at first glance.<br /><br />It's long, complicated, intricate, absorbing. Highly recommended, though I reluctantly concede that no, it's not for everyone. But, really, highly recommended.<br /><br />I bought this audiobook.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17253170814755072316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_665849376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665849376" />
    <a title="Andreas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas"><img alt="Andreas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512938270p2/20379307.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/665849376?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas">Andreas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=award-hugo">award-hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=award-locus">award-locus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665849376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15804050752732645728">Who killed Ari Emory? <br/>You won't find the final answer to this central question in this huge tome. But other topics like genetics, sexual abuse, or psychology are discussed intensely from different viewpoints. Most central is the broad theme of cloning (or psychogenesis, which is the exact cloning of body <b>and mind</b>) which makes it very relevant for current discussions of that theme. Mix it with lots of political scheming, homeopathic dosis of action, and a very bad tension arc to get this mileston</span>
  <span id="freeText15804050752732645728" style="display:none">Who killed Ari Emory? <br />You won't find the final answer to this central question in this huge tome. But other topics like genetics, sexual abuse, or psychology are discussed intensely from different viewpoints. Most central is the broad theme of cloning (or psychogenesis, which is the exact cloning of body <b>and mind</b>) which makes it very relevant for current discussions of that theme. Mix it with lots of political scheming, homeopathic dosis of action, and a very bad tension arc to get this milestone of Science Fiction. <br /><br />I think the novel would have deserved a far better and more conclusive ending, we shouldn't need to read the far later published <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3689197.Regenesis__Unionside___3_" title="Regenesis (Unionside, #3) by C.J. Cherryh" rel="nofollow noopener">Regenesis</a> to collect all the dangling ropes. In fact, the ending reads more like a short story's openness than a novel's closedness - it just stopped, no resolution or conclusion at all. When I said "homeopathic dosis of action", I referred to the first 95% of the novel - Cherryh spared the tension and action completely for the last couple of action. When I saw the end coming, I thought "oh no, it doesn't end, it doesn't end...", and so it did. What a cliffhanger!<br /><br />Cherryh touches lots of innovative futuristic topics like those human "slaves" called Azis or the concept of psychogenesis to name just a few. Instead of diving deeper into those topics, she concentrates on Ari II's coming-of-age story. I wouldn't say that her world-building was great.<br /><br />What I liked most about the novel was the innovative literaric figure of telling the story of Ari Emory by using the coming-of-age of her clone Ari II. Speaking of literaric figures, I wonder about her motivation to throw in huge amounts of religious phrases like "good God", "God", "I hope to God", "God knows", "My God" and similarily "hell". This is a sharp contrast to leaving out any discussion of religiosity. <br />Everything seems to be astonishingly instant as you can see from her frequent use of "sudden" or especially "of a sudden". She obviously tried to mimic the events' flows.<br />In general, I found the ridiculous amounts of phrases more annyoing than helpful.<br /><br />The same kind of distracting was an old problem of SF for me: Some of the used futuristic technology isn't valid any more. I don't have a problem with tapes, central computers, and absence of Internet or cell phones in older SF at all. The problem with Cherryh seems to be that she refers to them very often and develops ridiculous projections into the future. Just one example: Why should a huge computer take weeks to find something in the databasis when at the time of writing the start of her Alliance-Union series search algorithms were available on PCs retrieving information from MS Word documents instantly? <br /><br />I'd have loved to honour the work's complexity but it simply wasn't enough fun for me to give it more than 3 stars. Lots of quite confusing and unmotivating political schemes and discussions lead me to downgrading this enourmous work. On the one hand I can see that people would love it and it really deserved the 1989's Hugo and Locus awards. On the other hand I can also understand why others simply can't finish this slow story.<br /><br />2 1/2 stars rounded up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15804050752732645728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_696055897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696055897" />
    <a title="Charlie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4978224-charlie"><img alt="Charlie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435164846p2/4978224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696055897?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlie" href="/user/show/4978224-charlie">Charlie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4978224-charlie?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4978224-charlie?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4978224-charlie?shelf=female-protagonist">female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4978224-charlie?shelf=hugo-winner">hugo-winner</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696055897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15691713478322769541">When Ariane Emory (the first), head of Reseune genetic facilities, is murdered by Jordon Warrick, the next generation at Reseune has their shackles weakened just enough that they might be able to make a difference. Ariane Emory (the second), a replicate of Ariane Emory (the first), grows up in a tightly controlled environment with the hope that she will be just like her predecessor, but things don't work exactly as they hoped, she's starting where Ariane 1 left off, with the skill, instincts, an</span>
  <span id="freeText15691713478322769541" style="display:none">When Ariane Emory (the first), head of Reseune genetic facilities, is murdered by Jordon Warrick, the next generation at Reseune has their shackles weakened just enough that they might be able to make a difference. Ariane Emory (the second), a replicate of Ariane Emory (the first), grows up in a tightly controlled environment with the hope that she will be just like her predecessor, but things don't work exactly as they hoped, she's starting where Ariane 1 left off, with the skill, instincts, and knowledge, but with the determination to improve upon the legacy of Ariane 1. In particular Ariane 2 wants to make sure that Justin Warrick, Jordon's son and Ariane 1's victim, has the opportunity to achieve his potential and realize his dreams...under her benevolent leadership, of course. When politics don't stop and wait for Ariane 2 to grow up, she must walk a fine line between controlling and being controlled.<br /><br />In some ways Cyteen is the story of the murder of Ariane Emory, as the cover promises, but it is also much more than that. It is more the story of the ripples in the lives of a handful of people as her death creates a large empty space in the world. It's a story about power: The power that elder's have over youngers; that leaders have over successors; that mentally flexible people have over mentally rigid people; the power that love both gives and takes away.<br /><br />If all of that sounds like it is complicated and wide-ranging, you'd be correct. It isn't that this couldn't be boiled down to a Hollywood movie plot, it's more that Cherryh builds a level of intrigue and detail that would be ill-served when boiled down.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book for those that enjoy the complications of space operas, but wish they had a smaller cast.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15691713478322769541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1628796781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628796781" />
    <a title="Yefim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7002806-yefim"><img alt="Yefim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327120825p2/7002806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628796781?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yefim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yefim" href="/user/show/7002806-yefim">Yefim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/19043763-cyteen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=very-inspirational">very-inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=hugo-award">hugo-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=locus-award">locus-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=psychological-drama">psychological-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=sociological">sociological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=dystopias">dystopias</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7002806-yefim?shelf=mystery-and-thriller">mystery-and-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628796781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4560615698370324581">If “Brave New World” met The Gormenghast novels, this would be the offspring. Like Gormenghast, Cyteen is not an easy book to read. For one thing, it is very long book, at some 350,000 words. It is also a slow book- it covers two decades in Cherryh’s Alliance-Union universe. It is two bildungsroman in one, as it follows the two protagonists- Justin Warrick and Ariane Emory II- both clones of their parents, as they grow and adapt to their circumstances. The concept of nature vs nurture is at the </span>
  <span id="freeText4560615698370324581" style="display:none">If “Brave New World” met The Gormenghast novels, this would be the offspring. Like Gormenghast, Cyteen is not an easy book to read. For one thing, it is very long book, at some 350,000 words. It is also a slow book- it covers two decades in Cherryh’s Alliance-Union universe. It is two bildungsroman in one, as it follows the two protagonists- Justin Warrick and Ariane Emory II- both clones of their parents, as they grow and adapt to their circumstances. The concept of nature vs nurture is at the forefront, with people shaped by their environment. In fact, while the book is billed as a murder mystery, it is not- we don’t even discover the identity of the killer. Instead, the real mystery that keeps the reader glued to the pages is what will come out of all the manipulation, and whether the protagonists are able to transcend the flaws of their predecessors. The politics, the setting, the relationships between the characters are as complex and byzantine as anything by Peake. While no idea stands out as particularly original or brilliant, the central theme is so well-executed that it makes up for it in richness of detail. A superb work, overall. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4560615698370324581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50321782" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50321782" />
    <a title="Margaret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162759-margaret"><img alt="Margaret" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234732285p2/162759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50321782?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/162759-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=fantasy-and-science-fiction">fantasy-and-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=authors-cd">authors-cd</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50321782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1058587564941708496"><i>Cyteen</i> is a gripping and intense science fiction novel, set on the planet Cyteen in Cherryh's Merchanter Universe about 300 years in our future, when human cloning has become a reality. Ariane Emory is a brilliant scientist, and when she dies under mysterious circumstances, her successors create a replicate of Emory and struggle to duplicate her childhood environment as well, so that the replicate will grow up under the same conditions and become the same person; <i>Cyteen</i> is the story of the secon</span>
  <span id="freeText1058587564941708496" style="display:none"><i>Cyteen</i> is a gripping and intense science fiction novel, set on the planet Cyteen in Cherryh's Merchanter Universe about 300 years in our future, when human cloning has become a reality. Ariane Emory is a brilliant scientist, and when she dies under mysterious circumstances, her successors create a replicate of Emory and struggle to duplicate her childhood environment as well, so that the replicate will grow up under the same conditions and become the same person; <i>Cyteen</i> is the story of the second Ariane Emory. The characters are complex and their relationships intriguingly tortuous; the plot is intricate (and I feel that I'll probably get more of it on a re-read); and the world is very detailed and convincing. Although it was originally published fifteen years ago, Cherryh's exploration of genetics, environment, and nature vs. nurture continues to resonate and fascinate. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14156397" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14156397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12999466850277571124">If you have the slightest interest in the inner lives of smart children, the origins of personality, fictional politics, or human cloning, you should read this book.<br/><br/>If the central question of <i>Stand On Zanzibar</i> was "what does it mean to be human if we can't save ourselves?", the central question of <i>Cyteen</i> is "What does humanity mean when human minds can be made to order?"<br/><br/>That said, how much you enjoy it will depend on how attached you get to the characters and how well you can follow the often ob</span>
  <span id="freeText12999466850277571124" style="display:none">If you have the slightest interest in the inner lives of smart children, the origins of personality, fictional politics, or human cloning, you should read this book.<br /><br />If the central question of <i>Stand On Zanzibar</i> was "what does it mean to be human if we can't save ourselves?", the central question of <i>Cyteen</i> is "What does humanity mean when human minds can be made to order?"<br /><br />That said, how much you enjoy it will depend on how attached you get to the characters and how well you can follow the often obscure maneuvering of the various characters and factions. This is a book you'll like the first time but only really enjoy on rereading. It is not reader-friendly and you <i>will</i> work to enjoy it, but the reward is worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12999466850277571124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('naK+TdM/WejaN/VVfSKz2mXQnqpgwgLQftoRXxDBVItwtipxT0xhUgyPocoBsYfonrxgF+lDsyI6TTpUjBmFQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W18XkV+FKqbG3QPjm5qTBRuFSMS7FzVqL/WoFkwN5jy2S4Otw/YSHBBlV3znCac34Om2eTKWhJhrYoMd0NU39A==')})
  }
//]]>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_139986'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/139986.The_Snow_Queen?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Snow Queen (The Snow Queen Cycle, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/32279.Joan_D_Vinge?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Joan D. When famous adventurer Sir Richard Francis Burton dies, the last thing he expects to do is awaken naked on a foreign planet along the shores of a seemingly endless river. But that\'s where Burton and billions of other humans (plus a few nonhumans) find themselves as the epic Riverworld saga begins. It seems that all of Earthly humanity has been resurrected on the planet, each with an indestructible container that provides three meals a day, cigarettes, alcoholic beverages, a lighter, and the odd tube of lipstick. But why? And by whom? That\'s what Burton and a handful of fellow adventurers are determined to discover as they construct a boat and set out in search of the river\'s source, thought to be millions of miles away. Although there are many hardships during the journey--including an encounter with the infamous Hermann Goring--Burton\'s resolve to complete his quest is strengthened by a visit from the Mysterious Stranger, a being who claims to be a renegade within the very group that created the Riverworld. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10406692695573766716">Currently resident in Spokane, Washington, C.J. Cherryh has won four Hugos and is one of the best-selling and most critically acclaimed authors in the science fiction and fantasy field. She is the author of more than forty novels. Her hobbies include travel, photography, reef culture, Mariners baseball, and, a late passion, figure skating: she intends to compete in the adult USFSA track. She began</span>
  <span id="freeText10406692695573766716" style="display:none">Currently resident in Spokane, Washington, C.J. Cherryh has won four Hugos and is one of the best-selling and most critically acclaimed authors in the science fiction and fantasy field. She is the author of more than forty novels. Her hobbies include travel, photography, reef culture, Mariners baseball, and, a late passion, figure skating: she intends to compete in the adult USFSA track. She began with the modest ambition to learn to skate backwards and now is working on jumps. She sketches, occasionally, cooks fairly well, and hates house work; she loves the outdoors, animals wild and tame, is a hobbyist geologist, adores dinosaurs, and has academic specialties in Roman constitutional law and bronze age Greek ethnography. She has written science fiction since she was ten, spent ten years of her life teaching Latin and Ancient History on the high school level, before retiring to full time writing, and now does not have enough hours in the day to pursue all her interests. Her studies include planetary geology, weather systems, and natural and man-made catastrophes, civilizations, and cosmology…in fact, there's very little that doesn't interest her. A loom is gathering dust and needs rethreading, a wooden ship model awaits construction, and the cats demand their own time much more urgently. She works constantly, researches mostly on the internet, and has books stacked up and waiting to be written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10406692695573766716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/820134-cyteen">Quotes from Cyteen</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;He said sometimes when you're young you have to think about things, because you're forming your value-sets and you keep coming up with Data Insufficient and finding holes in your programs. So you keep trying to do a fix on your sets. And the more powerful your mind is and the more intense your concentration is, the worse damage you can do to yourself, which is why, Justin says, Alphas always have trouble and some of them go way off and out-there, and why almost all Alphas are eccentric. But he says the best thing you can do if you're too bright for your own good is what the Testers do, be aware where you got which idea, keep a tab on everything, know how your ideas link up with each other and with your deep-sets and value-sets, so when you're forty or fifty or a hundred forty and you find something that doesn't work, you can still find all the threads and pull them.<br /><br />But that's not real easy unless you know what your value-sets are, and most CITs don't. CITs have a trouble with not wanting to know that kind of thing. Because some of them are real eetee once you get to thinking about how they link. Especially about sex and ego-nets.<br /><br />Justin says inflexibility is a trap and most Alpha types are inward-turned because they process so fast they're gone and thinking before a Gamma gets a sentence out. Then they get in the habit of thinking they thought of everything, but they don't remember everything stems from input. You may have a new idea, but it stems from input somebody gave you, and that could be wrong or your senses could have been lying to you. He says it can be an equipment-quality problem or a program-quality problem, but once an Alpha takes a falsehood for true, it's a personal problem.&rdquo;</span>
